# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Java Service Initialization Lifecycle Pattern in Kafka

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle: the Lifecycle interface (or equivalent), the service startup ordering, and the coordinated shutdown sequence that ensures dependent services stop in reverse order.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

58-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Java service lifecycle pattern in Apache Kafka. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I've identified **18 core files** that implement the Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle pattern in Kafka, organized into three main categories:

### 1. **Core Server Lifecycle**
- **Server trait** (Server.scala) - Base abstraction with `startup()`, `shutdown()`, `awaitShutdown()`
- **KafkaRaftServer** - Entry point that orchestrates broker/controller startup and shutdown in correct order
- **BrokerServer** & **ControllerServer** - Implement the Server trait with complex startup sequences
- **SharedServer** - Manages shared components between broker and controller

### 2. **Raft & Scheduler Infrastructure**
- **KafkaRaftManager** - Manages Raft consensus with startup/shutdown lifecycle
- **Scheduler interface** - Java interface for background task scheduling with startup/shutdown methods
- **BrokerLifecycleManager** - Manages broker state transitions and registration with controller

### 3. **Connect Framework**
- **Connect, Herder, AbstractHerder** - Top-level lifecycle management
- **KafkaBasedLog** - Kafka topic-based logging with start/stop
- **Backing Stores** (KafkaOffsetBackingStore, FileOffsetBackingStore, etc.) - Persistent storage lifecycle

## Critical Design Pattern Features

1. **State Machine**: Uses `ProcessStatus` enum (SHUTDOWN, STARTING, STARTED, SHUTTING_DOWN) with atomic transitions
2. **Dependency Ordering**: Startup sequence ensures controller endpoints are available before broker starts
3. **Reverse Shutdown Order**: Dependencies are closed in reverse order of startup
4. **Exception Safety**: `CoreUtils.swallow()` ensures shutdown continues even if individual components fail
5. **Graceful Shu
... (truncated)

\n108: /**\n109:  * Abstract Herder implementation which handles connector/task lifecycle tracking. Extensions\n110:  * must invoke the lifecycle hooks appropriately.\n111:  * <p>\n112:  * This class takes the following approach for sending status updates to the backing store:\n113:  *\n114:  * <ol>\n115:  * <li>\n116:  *    When the connector or task is starting, we overwrite the previous state blindly. This ensures that\n117:  *    every rebalance will reset the state of tasks to the proper state. The intuition is that there should\n118:  *    be less chance of write conflicts when the worker has just received its assignment and is starting tasks.\n119:  *    In particular, this prevents us from depending on the generation absolutely. If the group disappears\n120:  *    and the generation is reset, then we'll overwrite the status information with the older (and larger)\n121:  *    generation with the updated one. The danger of this approach is that slow starting tasks may cause the\n122:  *    status to be overwritten after a rebalance has completed.\n123:  *\n124:  * <li>\n125:  *    If the connector or task fails or is shutdown, we use {@link StatusBackingStore#putSafe(ConnectorStatus)},\n126:  *    which provides a little more protection if the worker is no longer in the group (in which case the\n127:  *    task may have already been started on another worker). Obviously this is still racy. If the task has just\n128:  *    started on another worker, we may not have the updated status cached yet. In this case, we'll overwrite\n129:  *    the value which will cause the state to be inconsistent (most likely until the next rebalance). Until\n130:  *    we have proper producer groups with fenced groups, there is not much else we can do.\n131:  * </ol>\n132:  */\n133: public abstract class AbstractHerder implements Herder, TaskStatus.Listener, ConnectorStatus.Listener {\n134: \n135:     private static final Logger log = LoggerFactory.getLogger(AbstractHerder.class);\n136: \n137:     private final String workerId;\n138: Shuts down BrokerServer first (may need controller for controlled shutdown)\\n2. Then shuts down ControllerServer\\n3. Unregisters app info\\n\\n**BrokerServer.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala:729-820) follows strict sequence:\\n1. Metadata publishers cleanup\\n5. Request handler pool shutdown\\n6. Scheduler shutdown (CRITICAL - before LogManager to prevent concurrent operations)\\n7. LogManager shutdown\\n8. ReplicaManager shutdown\\n9. Coordinator shutdown\\n10. Final resource cleanup\\n\\n**ControllerServer.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ControllerServer.scala:126) shuts down:\\n1. SocketServer\\n2. QuorumController\\n3. Metadata publishers\\n4. Request handlers\\n5. Quota managers\\n\\n**RaftManager.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/raft/RaftManager.scala:171-179) cleanly closes:\\n1. Expiration service\\n2. Client driver\\n3. Scheduler\\n4. Network channel\\n5. Replicated log\\n6. Data directory locks\\n\\n## Java Scheduler Interface\\n\\nThe `Scheduler` interface (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java:27) defines the pattern:\\n- `void startup()` - Initialize scheduler\\n- `void shutdown() throws InterruptedException` - Stop all scheduled tasks\\n\\n## Connect Framework Lifecycle\\n\\nKafka Connect implements similar patterns:\\n\\n**Connect** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Connect.java:35):\\n- `start()` - Starts herder, REST server, and shutdown hook\\n- `stop()` - Stops herder and REST server\\n- `awaitStop()` - Blocks until shutdown complete\\n\\n**Herder** interface (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Herder.java:63-68):\\n- `void start()` - Creates producer/consumer, reads to log end, starts work thread\\n- `stop()` - Signals stop, joins thread, closes clients\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **State Machine**: ProcessStatus enum (SHUTDOWN, STARTING, STARTED, SHUTTING_DOWN) with atomic transitions\\n2. **Dependency Ordering**: Strict startup sequence ensures dependencies are ready before dependent components start\\n3. **Reverse Shutdown**: Shutdown follows reverse of startup order to safely close dependent services first\\n4. **Exception Safety**: Uses CoreUtils.swallow() to continue shutdown despite exceptions\\n5. **Locking**: ReentrantLock and condition variables coordinate state transitions and await shutdown\\n6. **Timeouts**: Deadline-based timeouts prevent indefinite blocking during startup/shutdown\\n7. **Coordinated Startup**: SharedServer.startForBroker()/startForController() ensure single initialization of shared components\\n8. **Graceful Shutdown**: Controlled shutdown protocol allows clean hand-off of responsibilities before hard stop\"\n}\n",

MetadataLoader processes metadata updates\\n\\n## Shutdown Sequence (Reverse Order)\\n\\n**KafkaRaftServer.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaRaftServer.scala:100-107) orchestrates shutdown:\\n1. Shuts down BrokerServer first (may need controller for controlled shutdown)\\n2. Then shuts down ControllerServer\\n3. Unregisters app info\\n\\n**BrokerServer.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala:729-820) follows strict sequence:\\n1. Optionally begins controlled shutdown (replicaManager and lifecycleManager)\\n2. Begins shutdown of BrokerLifecycleManager\\n3. Stops socket server request processors\\n4. Metadata publishers cleanup\\n5. Request handler pool shutdown\\n6. Scheduler shutdown (CRITICAL - before LogManager to prevent concurrent operations)\\n7. LogManager shutdown\\n8. ReplicaManager shutdown\\n9. Coordinator shutdown\\n10. Final resource cleanup\\n\\n**ControllerServer.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ControllerServer.scala:126) shuts down:\\n1. SocketServer\\n2. QuorumController\\n3. Metadata publishers\\n4. Request handlers\\n5. Quota managers\\n\\n**RaftManager.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/raft/RaftManager.scala:171-179) cleanly closes:\\n1. Expiration service\\n2. Client driver\\n3. Scheduler\\n4. Network channel\\n5. Replicated log\\n6. Data directory locks\\n\\n## Java Scheduler Interface\\n\\nThe `Scheduler` interface (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java:27) defines the pattern:\\n- `void startup()` - Initialize scheduler\\n- `void shutdown() throws InterruptedException` - Stop all scheduled tasks\\n\\n## Connect Framework Lifecycle\\n\\nKafka Connect implements similar patterns:\\n\\n**Connect** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Connect.java:35):\\n- `start()` - Starts herder, REST server, and shutdown hook\\n- `stop()` - Stops herder and REST server\\n- `awaitStop()` - Blocks until shutdown complete\\n\\n**Herder** interface (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Herder.java:63-68):\\n- `void start()` - Start herder\\n- `void stop()` - Stop herder\\n\\n**AbstractHerder** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/AbstractHerder.java:180-192):\\n- `startServices()` - Starts worker, statusBackingStore, configBackingStore\\n- `stopServices()` - Stops services in reverse order, shuts down executor\\n\\n**Backing Stores** implement consistent lifecycle:\\n- KafkaOffsetBackingStore.start() (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/KafkaOffsetBackingStore.java:231) starts internal offsetLog\\n- KafkaOffsetBackingStore.stop() (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/KafkaOffsetBackingStore.java:260) stops offsetLog\\n- FileOffsetBackingStore implements similar pattern\\n\\n**KafkaBasedLog** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/util/KafkaBasedLog.java:220-286):\\n- `start()` - Creates producer/consumer, reads to log end, starts work thread\\n- `stop()` - Signals stop, joins thread, closes clients\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **State Machine**: ProcessStatus enum (SHUTDOWN, STARTING, STARTED, SHUTTING_DOWN) with atomic transitions\\n2. **Dependency Ordering**: Strict startup sequence ensures dependencies are ready before dependent components start\\n3. **Reverse Shutdown**: Shutdown follows reverse of startup order to safely close dependent services first\\n4. **Exception Safety**: Uses CoreUtils.swallow() to continue shutdown despite exceptions\\n5. **Locking**: ReentrantLock and condition variables coordinate state transitions and await shutdown\\n6. **Timeouts**: Deadline-based timeouts prevent indefinite blocking during startup/shutdown\\n7. **Coordinated Startup**: SharedServer.startForBroker()/startForController() ensure single initialization of shared components\\n8. **Graceful Shutdown**: Controlled shutdown protocol allows clean hand-off of responsibilities before hard stop\"\n}\n",
